<user_id>103859381351358786121</user_id><Text>Middling food, high price, poor experience.

Seoul Sausage is a Korean + Sausage fusion restaurant. Dishes include Kalbi sausage with kimchi relish, chicken sausage, Korean fried chicken, and others (the menu was not fully built out yet. Combos include a can of soda and tater tots for $3 extra. You order using a tablet.

First, the food. My group tried everything that was available on the menu (the restaurant was not fully stocked since it literally JUST opened): Kalbi sausage with kimchi relish, chicken sausage, Korean fried chicken, and the tater tots. These were all... fine. Nothing really to write home about. The Kalbi sausage with Kimchi relish should have been a wow, but it could have just as easily been a bratwurst. The chicken sausage was a sweeter version of andoiulle sausage. I was unimpressed. The fried chicken was better, but needed something to go with it to balance the dish. And the tater tots were, well, tater tots. For the price ($8 for 1 small sausage on a bun) we expected to get something substantial or something that really WOWed us.

The experience. I couldn't stand the experience. Cold, detached, and not friendly. The user orders for themselves using a small terminal, but nobody saw that you had to do this. The terminals just looked like point of sale terminals, not self service kiosks. I didn't see any signage for it, either. The kitchen is open, and the chefs are right there to look at you, but they didn't help either. The presentation was a little weak - the food came in simple paper cartons and drinks are just cans of soda.

To sum up, Seoul Sausage has many of the trappings of a food truck - fusion fare, loud noise, sort of rude staff, cans of coke, high prices - but none of the charm or exceptional food.< /Text></record></dataset><record>

<GmapID>0x808580bed9afabe3:0x6984b39ba244b968< /GmapID><Review>We ended up here for a late lunch (1-2pm) because every other restaurant in Japantown was full with a wait.  We were so surprised that it was empty, and wondered if it was a bad sign.  Reviews were mediocre, but we decided to give it a try and were NOT disappointed.  This was our first experience at a Korean BBQ, and the waitress, who knew plenty of English, was really patient with us and very helpful in choosing dishes.

I have read some reviews that said children are not welcome here.  We had our 4 year old and 7 year old boys with us, and the waitress was very kind to them, and helpful in choosing dishes that they might like based on their dietary preferences!  We all enjoyed the beef bulgogi and side dishes as well as the noodle soup.  I would definitely recommend this restaurant to friends visiting Japantown!< /Review></record>

<Time>1482817552220< /Time><rate>2< /rate><Text>Holy Moly this place was *cheap* despite of seemingly expensive look of the set up. Service was cheap, attitude was cheap, quality was cheap and I am still scratching my head for the reason why I went to this eatery.

OK back to the full course (BBQ table). We came here with a high expectation of better food and service due to its higher price tags on the menu compared to EVERY other Korean BBQ places we've visited in the past and boy I was so wrong on this. The only time when we were attended was at the entrance by the restaurant owner/manager and the experience just went downhill from there. During the ordering, the waiter only said what you *must* and what you *cannot* do. For instance, in order to sit by the BBQ table, one has to order at least 2 overpriced meats and they would not change your charred smoking grate until you beg so and here's the catch, they would only allow to change 2 times and that's why if you let them do your BBQ, they would just *pour* everything on the grate to save their time and trouble. There are a lot of other hidden rules that you would probably not notice until it's too late. During the whole dinner time (about 45 mins), no waiter/waitress came to say anything except when we asked for a new grate, and they did not refill any of our water/tea, nor our sides. The only interesting interaction was when I stopped the waitress from pouring everything into the grate, she aggressively handed over the tongs and pushed plates under my right elbow. However they became super *attentive* when it's near the end of the course and ready for the check. They would literally check your seat every minute to see if you have placed the credit card yet or not and couldn't wait to see you go after everything's done. What a contrast.

In regard to the food, it's OK and that's the reason I gave it a 2 star instead of 1. However the food is severely overpriced by about 50% and you couldn't even find a an appetizer that's less than $10. Every BBQ entry  (about 10 oz meat + lettuce) is from $30 to $50 and the quality is just so so. I've been to other much cheaper places where both food quality and service were superior. I would not recommend anyone who has a second choice to go here. You could probably have a better ROI of your poor $70+ on lottery- at least you could daydream a few days right?

Oh here's another interesting fact. The menu posted at their entrance does not reflect the true prices on the actual menu because they've bumped the actual prices a few times. Another interesting finding is that their actual menus are not consistent either. Some menus have salad-#8 option while the others do not.

Anyway, San Francisco in its own is a beautiful and charming city in our experience. This place, however, is a such disgrace to it.< /Text>< pics>

I did a lot of research before speaking with any solar suppliers, as the subject was new  to me. Then I contacted four suppliers, two large and two small, and requested a plan and bid to install solar in our 5,750 sq ft home in Rancho Santa Fe. Dave Watt, owner and operator of Solar Watt was included, as he had been recommended to me by my roofer who I have done business with for thirteen years. After speaking in detail with each of the four suppliers, Solar Watt was an easy choice.

Dave asked for the information from my electric bill which he needed to develop a plan and then came to the house and showed me four alternatives, clearly explaining each in a very accurate manner. (The two big suppliers told me things I knew to be incorrect and tried to sell me a larger system then I needed.They were also more expensive. The other small supplier offered a slightly lower cost but could not answer several of my questions about the system they were proposing).

Dave handled all of the paperwork including the permits and tie in to the electric company.

Certainly one of the best suppliers I have ever worked with. Feel free to ask Dave to provide you with my name as a reference.</Text>

< text>
We were having some issues with our Enphase Solar system connecting to our wi-fi network, and since the company who had done the install for the previous owner of our house was no longer providing service I went to the Enphase website to find another installer/service provider who might be able to help.  I found Solar Watt Solutions on the Enphase website and gave them a call.  The gentlemen with whom I spoke was very professional and courteous and let me know one of his technicians would give me a call within a couple of days.

Dave Watt gave me a call and spent almost an hour on the phone with me walking me through what needed to be done.  I finally got it connected and then later that night I saw that not all of the microinverters were sending data.  I called Enphase customer support and after some trouble-shooting the lady suggested I call my installer.  So I called Dave again and he walked me through a few steps until we got it figured out and fixed.  And all of this at no charge.

In my mind that is next-level customer service to provide that level of service to someone who isn't even your customer.  He very easily could have scheduled a service call and come out and charged me for what he did.  I would definitely recommend Solar Watt Solutions to anyone looking for a top notch solar company.< /text>

<time>1522953377567</time><rate>5<//rate>< text>
This place is a solid breakfast and lunch place for locals and tourists alike. Starting with breakfast, they have a wide selection of coffee and tea drinks. The breakfast sandwiches (design however you please), breakfast rice (amazing to go option and even better as hangover food), and the pastry/mini pie collection all provide ample breakfast options. The lunch selection is mostly sandwich based. The grilled chicken pesto sandwich (pictured) is AMAZEBALLS in the best of ways! Who would have thought a huge grilled red pepper, mustard, and pesto would have made such a good flavor combo, right? This is not a fancy brunch spot, but it is a great place for friends to meet for breakfast or lunch.< /text>

<rate>5</rate>< Review>
Nice place. I love it here. There is both indoor and outdoor seating where you can bring your dog.
Coffee is self serve and really good.
The omelettes are outstanding and they have lots of other choices as well such as pancakes, scrambles, kids choices.
To park you have to go around the corner, or you can park before the bridge and have a nice walk across it.
Plenty of flowers outside so if you sit out it's really nice to look at and smells good !!
Get the Florentine omelette!
Servers are friendly. There is free Wi-Fi and across the street is a farmstand with fresh produce.</Review>

< Review>
On our trip, we made a stop at Half Moon Bay to walk the touristy shops on main street and we ducked into the Half Moon Bay Coffee Company for some lunch.   What a great decision this was.    They have both a great breakfast (which is served all day) and lunch/dinner menu.   A good number of selections available on both.    Here, you stand in line to place your orders, and they give you an order and bring the food to your table.   I choose a patti melt and my husband had a ruebin.   Both were delicious.  Only complaint, if I had to come up with one, is the glass of ice tea was very small and if refills were available, it was not expressed.

They also have a great array of desserts in the case that looked delicious and at reasonable prices for their size (I mean delicious looking concoctions !!!).   But, my jeans are getting tight, so had to pass on them.   The coffee also smelled delicious.

I highly recommend this stop.</Review>
